Chinese Troops Control the Suburbs of Jiangmen and Xinhui; Japanese Troops' Attempt to Invade Samshui Fails; Japanese Troops in Shunde Are Transferred to Support Jiangmen and Xinhui; Zhongshan Suffers Extremely Severe Disasters Due to Devastation 48

Hong Kong correspondence: The Japanese troops invading Xinzeng and Jiangmen in Guangdong Province have recently threatened to invade Samshui, the commercial center of the central district, and have advanced along the Xin Kai road line. On the 27th, 28th, and 30th of last month, Japanese aircraft repeatedly bombed Samshui, and the ferries of Xinhui, Kaiping, Taishan, and Enping were also attacked by Japanese aircraft, intending to assist the Japanese troops in advancing rapidly. However, by the 31st, large numbers of Chinese troops had successively reinforced along the Xin Kai road line and engaged in fierce battles with the Japanese troops in the vicinity of Da Xiao Mei and Lian Tang. The Japanese troops were defeated, leaving dozens of corpses, and retreated in a mess back to Xinhui. The Chinese troops took advantage of the victory and pursued, and have recovered Da Xiao Mei. The Japanese troops defended stubbornly, firing cannons at the Shatidi Bridge and Jinniu Mountain west of the city. There was also contact between the two armies near the Fenjiang River, but the fighting was not as intense as before. There were no major battles on the Xinhe, Jiangfo, and Jiangzhuo roads. The Japanese troops stubbornly defended Jiangmen, and its suburbs have been controlled by Chinese troops. The situation in Samshui has also eased. Many of the ferries in Siyi have also resumed service, but after passing Sanjiang, they still need to be transferred by long boats. However, the Japanese troops' ambition to invade has not been curbed. It is recently heard that the Japanese troops in Daliang, Rongqi, Guizhou, and other places in Shunde have also been transferred to reinforce Jiangmen and Xinhui, but the number of people is unknown. At present, the majority of the Japanese troops in Jiangmen and Xinhui are concentrated in the vicinity of Xin Kai Road and Licun area of Jiang Fo Road near Xinhui. The Second Detachment of the First Guerrilla Area recently attacked Daliang, Rongqi, Guizhou, and other places in Shunde and was very successful. The former Xinshun Special Detachment of the Fifth Guerrilla Area, the Zhou Hanling Department, also carried out night attacks on Japanese troops on the river surface at the intersection of Xinshun. At that time, a Japanese ship traveling to Guangzhou and Jiangmen passed by and was intercepted by the unit, fighting each other for several hours, killing many Japanese and puppet troops.

The Japanese navy previously invaded Zhongshan, Hengmen, Dieshi, Jinzhong, and other places and was severely attacked by the Chinese local troops, suffering heavy casualties. The army also suffered considerable losses. According to a military intelligence report yesterday, the bodies of the Japanese navy officers and soldiers killed in action have been completely transported back to Guangzhou for cremation. Peng Dongyuan, chairman of the puppet Guangdong Security Committee, actually led a group of people to hold a memorial service for the Japanese navy officers and soldiers killed in action in the large open space in front of the Japanese naval headquarters on the 29th of last month. Japanese military officers also attended the ceremony. As for Zhongshan County, which has been repeatedly devastated by Japanese troops, the damage is enormous. The first, second, and fourth districts have become fields of rubble and scorched earth, with desolate scenes. At present, disaster victims are everywhere, suffering from hunger and cold. In addition, they have lost their homes and are living in the open, or they are suffering from serious illnesses and moaning. They lament the lack of livelihood and feel that it is difficult to prolong their lingering lives. They are displaced and cannot be described. According to statistics, more than 500 people were killed by Japanese troops or died of fright. More than 2,300 houses were destroyed, and more than 2,700 households were robbed. The people's property losses totaled more than 2,917,170 yuan. More than 1,650 women were insulted. The suffering of the disaster is truly unbearable to speak of. In Bao'an County, Japanese troops have been strengthening the defensive works in Nantou, Shenzhen, and other places for days to prevent Chinese troops from counterattacking. They have also laid landmines on the Baoshen, Yankou, and Shashen roads. In addition, the airfield that the Japanese troops previously built in the wasteland behind the Tianmian Village on the Baoshen Road has now been suspended because it is not suitable for military use. At 6:00 am one day, the Japanese artillery team in Shenzhen Datouling fired two or thirty shells in succession. The Japanese troops in Shenzhen were preparing one after another. Later, it was learned that the Japanese artillery in Datouling had mistakenly thought that the Chinese troops were attacking and fired cannons to prevent it. At present, the Japanese troops in Bao'an all stay in defensive works and trenches at night, and only come out to act during the day. Every morning, they must fire cannons into the air. The Chinese troops are well aware that the morale of the Japanese troops is depressed and have sent teams to completely encircle the periphery of the Japanese troops in Bao'an, cutting off the Japanese troops' transportation lines and waiting for an opportunity to attack.

Rampant Pirate Activity in Fujian Province's Wu Islet, Coordinating with Japanese Forces; Military Authorities Maintain Strict Defense 49

Fuzhou Correspondence: Since the start of the War of Resistance, several coastal islands in Fujian Province have fallen. In the southern Fujian region, these include Jinmen (Quemoy), Xiamen (Amoy), and Meizhou islands. In the Fujian-Guangdong region, there are Pingtan, Chuanshi, Dongsha, and Nangan islands. Of these, Jinmen, Xiamen, and Chuanshi islands are garrisoned by Japanese troops. Pingtan, Meizhou, Dongsha, and Nangan islands are occupied by pirates under Japanese command. Puppet organizations have been established on Jinmen, Xiamen, and Pingtan islands, with Chinese traitors serving as puppet county magistrates and puppet mayors. The pirates call themselves the "Fujian People's Army" and specialize in raiding the coastal areas and waters of Fuqing, Lianjiang, Changle, Putian, Xianyou, and Hui'an counties, seizing young men, women, grain, money, which they exchange with the Japanese army for weapons. At the same time, the Japanese army also lays mines at various harbors to prohibit ships from entering and exiting, in order to blockade the province's economy. However, because the Chinese defenses are very strict, the Japanese army and pirates, despite repeated attempts to launch joint incursions, have been unable to advance onto the mainland. Since mid-August, the Japanese side has mobilized naval and air forces to launch large-scale attacks on Dongshan Island in southern Fujian. More than ten attacks have been repelled by the defending troops, inflicting heavy casualties. These casualties are being continuously transported back to Taiwan from Xiamen for burial and treatment. The offensive has stalled. The number of Japanese warships along the coast has also greatly decreased compared to May and June. The two important ports of Fuzhou and Quanzhou are usually without any Japanese warship sightings. If one or two ships arrive, they leave after only a few hours. Only the waters off Xiamen often have twelve or thirteen Japanese warships anchored. Therefore, foreign ships from Shanghai and Hong Kong can occasionally enter, and the prices of cloth, medicine, cotton yarn, and oil have gradually fallen. However, Japanese goods are often mixed in. Recently, in the Hanjiang area, a batch of Japanese goods worth more than one million yuan was seized. The pirates occupying Meizhou Island have been repeatedly repelled by the Chinese army but seize opportunities to invade again. Currently, a portion of the island is still occupied by pirates, who use it as a base to harass the coasts of Putian, Xianyou, Fuqing, and Hui'an counties. Therefore, the military authorities have ordered a blockade of the coasts of the above four counties, strictly prohibiting ships from traveling to and from Meizhou, under the penalty of being treated as collaborators. Foreign ships are also prohibited from entering and exiting the Xiuyu port of Hui'an and the Haikou port of Fuqing. On the other hand, the coastal district governments of Fuqing, Putian, Xianyou, and Hui'an are ordered to strictly inspect household registrations. The district governments, together with the garrison troops, are responsible for ensuring that each Lianbao (collective security unit) conducts an inspection every week, and, according to the Baojia system, the residence and movement of people should be accurately registered to prevent bandits and traitors from hiding among them.

Military Affairs Commission Announces Weekly War Situation, From the 1st to the 7th of This Month (Continued from Yesterday) 50

Guangdong Front: In Sanshui, Xijiang, on the mornings of the 3rd and 4th, the Japanese forces advanced towards Yangmei through Xinan town. The Chinese forces used mobile tactics to surround and severely attack the Japanese troops. By noon, the Japanese forces broke through and retreated to Sanshui. The Chinese forces took advantage of the victory to pursue them, inflicting many casualties. On the 6th, our air force attacked Guangzhou and encountered Japanese aircraft while passing through Sanshui, resulting in a fierce air battle. Three Japanese aircraft were shot down, and another three were heavily damaged and fled. As for the Japanese forces in Jiangmen and Xinhui, on the morning of the 4th, they launched an attack on Duruan under the cover of artillery fire. The Chinese forces calmly responded and fought for half a day before the Japanese forces retreated along their original route, leaving countless corpses behind. In the Chao'an area of the East River, on the dawn of the 5th, the Japanese forces, under the cover of artillery fire, launched attacks on Yixi from both Zhuxiang and Shibei. The Chinese army fiercely resisted, and the battle lasted until 4 PM. Yixi was briefly lost but was subsequently recaptured through counterattacks from multiple routes, engaging in hand-to-hand combat until 8 PM. Zhuxiang and Shibei were also captured. The Japanese suffered heavy losses. On the Southern front, the Japanese forces trapped on Qionghai (Hainan) Island and in Wenchang have been under constant attack by the Chinese forces in recent days, resulting in numerous Japanese deaths. The remaining Japanese forces in the city are now retreating to Haikou. The Japanese forces at the two strongholds of Donggu Tan and Niujiao Tang in the county are also tightly surrounded by the Chinese forces and are attempting to escape.

Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Fronts: In Jiangnan, after the county seat of Yixing was recaptured by the Chinese forces on the 21st of last month, the remaining Japanese forces retreated towards Heqiao and Caoqiao. This week, two thousand reinforcements were sent from the Shanghai-Hangzhou area to launch a large-scale counterattack and launched multiple attacks, resulting in fierce battles. Heqiao has now also been captured by the Chinese forces, who are advancing towards Liyang, where fierce battles are taking place. The Japanese forces trapped near Zha Port in Pudong were besieged by the Chinese army on the 4th, resulting in the killing of hundreds of soldiers. The remaining Japanese forces are wavering. In Wukang and Yuhang in western Zhejiang, more than 1,800 Japanese troops have been fiercely attacking Changsu and Yangjiatou for days, engaging in fierce battles with the Chinese army. The Japanese have not succeeded so far. Another unit of the Chinese army attacked the Japanese forces in Zhapu, recapturing the area and surrounding Pinghu, advancing towards Jiaxing and Xie Shi, and completely controlling the Shanghai-Hangzhou railway. In Guichi in southern Anhui, the Japanese forces launched a fierce attack towards Beishan in the east. On the morning of the 2nd, the area was briefly lost but was recaptured by a sudden counterattack by the Chinese forces at noon, forcing the Japanese to retreat. Continuous mopping-up operations have completely recovered all the strongholds near Guichi, including Sihailing, Pingdingshan, and Lanshan, and are now advancing towards Yin Jia Hui. Shuang Gou He and Liu Ji in northern Anhui were also captured by the Chinese forces on the evening of the 1st, forcing the remaining Japanese forces to retreat towards Huaiyuan.

In addition, Ke'anbei in western Suiyuan and Elu Humm and Chou Sih Hao were captured, as well as Ma Mier and Nan Bao Guan Jing near Baotou. In southern Hebei, Heng Ru Zan Huang besieged Ji County. In northern Shandong, Li Jin was captured, Heng Tai was besieged, and Xia Jin was pressured, resulting in the death of many Japanese officers, including Senior Officer Nakamura. In northern Hunan, Xinkai Tang near Yueyang was briefly captured, and the Japanese transportation between Linxiang and Yueyang was cut off. There were also attacks on the county seats of Jing'an, Xin Jian, and Wu Ning, resulting in numerous casualties. On the 4th, Japanese aircraft in the skies near Chengdu were severely attacked by our heroic air force, and Commander Okuda of the Japanese Naval Air Force was killed. These are all important achievements of the past week and are reported here as an addendum. (9th dispatch)

Jiangyin Puppet Bureau Chief Chen Zubei Arrested; Insatiable Greed and Accumulated Wealth 51

Jiangyin Correspondence: Chen Zubei, a native of Jiangyin, residing in Qiaoqi Town, served as the chairman of the puppet self-government association when Jiangyin fell. Shanghai: A Glimpse of Talent Supply and Demand Two Years After the War (II) Pan Wen'an, Zheng Wenhan, Shen Guanglie 55

Most job seekers are young, which is very clear from Table 2. Combining men and women, 81% are aged between 15 and 30. Separately, the largest group is between 21 and 25, which is roughly similar to the situation a year after the war. However, among women, the age of job seekers is gradually increasing to over 20, indicating an increasing trend of married women pursuing careers. There is also an increasing trend of young people aged 15 to 20, who, due to economic difficulties, are forced to leave school and struggle in society during their educational years. There are still quite a few adults seeking employment, an increase of 1% compared to the previous year.

Age Classification of Job Seekers (Table 2) The educational level of job seekers is concentrated among young people who have graduated from or attended secondary schools, accounting for 51.7% of the total. The next largest group is job seekers with vocational school or primary school education, accounting for 23.8%. The smallest group is job seekers with higher education, accounting for 14.9%. Compared with the previous year, there is an increasing trend in job seekers with primary school education, while there has been a significant decrease in those with university education. The reason is that there is an urgent need for talents with university and specialized education in the inland areas, and there has been a significant increase in those serving in the rear. Very few illiterate job seekers register at the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center, so this statistic can only represent the general situation of educated job seekers.

Attempts to Obstruct the Import of Legal Tender Fail: False Supervisor's Conspiracy Foiled, Claiming the Intention Was to Manage, Not Prohibit; Foreign Exchange Rates Ease and Legal Tender Value Rises for Several Days 69

After Li Jiannan, the "Supervisor of the Jianghai Customs," attempted to obstruct the import of Chinese legal tender, consuls from various countries and foreign banks firmly opposed it and ignored him. The supervisor then proposed to manage the transportation of legal tender, claiming it was due to legitimate needs, stating that importing legal tender should require his prior permission. However, foreign banks also decided to ignore this so-called "management." As for Luo, the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, he never issued an order to prohibit or manage it. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency learned from banking circles yesterday that "the supervisor's" attempt to obstruct the import of legal tender was aimed at promoting his "Huaxing Notes." The so-called management was also a method of obstruction because the "Huaxing Notes" claimed to be pegged to the British pound at a rate of sixpence. Therefore, the exchange rate announced daily by one of the tax collection offices of the Jianghai Customs showed the "Huaxing Notes" to be higher than the legal tender. Now, because the Shanghai foreign exchange black market has eased, the British pound is close to sixpence, and the price of legal tender will be higher than the "Huaxing Notes," causing a great blow to the "Huaxing Notes." Therefore, he attempted to obstruct legal tender to promote fluctuations in the foreign exchange black market and used the prevention of legal tender inflation as a pretext. In reality, the issuance of Chinese legal tender has always been cautious, and cash reserves remain sufficient. The government has never resorted to paper money policies, and there is no inflation.

The "North China Daily News" reported that yesterday (the 9th), it was heard from responsible sources that Li Jiannan, the customs supervisor recently appointed by the "new government," sent a letter to the consuls of the Shanghai Consular Body, which did not mention "prohibiting" the import and export of banknotes from Chinese banks but aimed at "controlling the monetary actions of banks." The Consular Body has not yet responded to Li's letter.

Not Obstructing the Import of Legal Tender

Li Jiannan recently told reporters that there had been a misunderstanding regarding the news of his letter to the consuls, which he deeply regretted. His purpose was not to prohibit the import and export of legal tender but only to control the banks and allow them the monetary actions of foreign banks transporting large amounts of legal tender to Shanghai. Banks engaged in transporting currency to Shanghai could achieve their goals if they first applied to him for "permission."

So-called Appropriate Utilization

Furthermore, if the imported legal tender is put to appropriate use, permission will be granted. This matter is mostly related to foreign banks because Chinese banks have not transported amounts of legal tender to Shanghai large enough to attract his attention. The original intent of this order was to seek the "welfare of the Shanghai market and trade," as too many banknotes would cause "inflation," he said. When asked by reporters if there were any difficulties in implementing control, Li replied that this was another question.

The Rumor of Control is Also Inaccurate

The "Shanghai Times" reported that Li Jiannan firmly denied yesterday that the "Reformed Government" had prohibited the import and export of legal tender in Shanghai, and said that the rumor that the customs authorities are now taking a method of controlling currency is not accurate. The regulations issued do not prohibit the import and export of legal tender but broadly state that the actions of currency must be controlled. Therefore, what is now being taken is a method of control, not prohibition.

The Puppet Regime's Purpose is to Apply First

Last year, there were various unrestricted actions of importing and exporting silver. Now, large amounts of banknotes are being transferred, mostly transported in and out of Hong Kong. In his letter to the consular leader, he outlined the regulations that must be followed and explained that the secret transportation of legal tender is not allowed. Whether Chinese or foreign banks wish to import or export legal tender for commercial purposes, they must first apply for permission from the "Customs Supervisor." The banks must prove that this legal tender is for their own business operations. If the "Customs" considers that the regulations have been followed and that the funds are not used for market speculation, permission will be granted.

Chase Bank's Banknotes Were Never Detained

The letter to the consuls was written in Chinese and dated October 4th, urging the banks to comply with the regulations for the benefit of themselves and the Shanghai market and trade. In response to the matter of the President Pierce's ship carrying approximately 10 million yuan of banknotes last week being briefly detained, Li said that Chase Bank had applied for permission to import these banknotes when they were first transported. The customs opened the boxes for inspection when the legal tender arrived at the customs dock and eventually passed them through.

Polish People All Over the World Celebrate National Day

November 11th is Armistice Day of the World War, which is also Poland's National Day. After being ruled by foreign countries for 150 years, Poland regained its independence on November 11, 1918. Polish people all over the world will celebrate National Day tomorrow (the 11th). According to news from the Polish Consulate, the

Polish Embassy

will hold a reception tomorrow from 11:30 to 12:30, and has invited Polish expatriates and diplomatic personnel from various countries to attend. In addition, there are various other activities. Historically, Poland occupied an important position in Eastern European politics for 800 years from 902 to 1795. It was then subjected to

Three Partitions

by powerful neighbors in 1772, etc. During the World War from 1914 to 1918, after Germany and Austria suffered defeats, Poland declared its independence on November 11, 1919. On this day, the late General Pilsudski formally notified various countries of the existence of the Polish nation. In the subsequent 21 years, Poland made progress in all aspects and was

Recognized by Various Countries

In September of this year, Germany invaded Poland and occupied its territory. Poland has to fight again to resist aggression. Now that the Allied countries are assisting in the military to restore the Polish nation, Poland can be expected to rise again and be even stronger.

The eighth repayment of principal for the 25th Year of the Republic of China Unified Public Bond, Series D, and the ninth repayment of principal for the 23rd Year of the Republic of China Yu Ping Railway Public Bond was drawn yesterday at 10:00 a.m. Pei Yunqing of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Hu Xiqian of the Bankers Association, Shen Jingliang of the Money Dealers Association, Hu Chao of the Shanghai First Special District Court, Fan Jietang of the National Debt Fund Management Committee, Wang Lin of the Central Bank, Tang Yusun of the Bank of China, and Fan Chuchen of the Bank of Communications attended. Chairman's Report

The drawing method for the Unified Public Bond uses the last three digits of the number, and the drawing method for the Yu Ping Railway Public Bond uses the last two digits of the number. Now, I will briefly report to you the situation of the above public bonds. The Unified Public Bond, Series D, was issued in February of the 25th Year of the Republic of China, with a fixed amount of 550 million yuan in national currency. This repayment is the eighth, with eight branches of 550,000 yuan each, for a total repayment of 4.4 million yuan. The Yu Ping Railway Public Bond was issued in June of the 23rd Year of the Republic of China, with a fixed amount of 12 million yuan in national currency. This repayment is the ninth, with seven branches of 120,000 yuan each, for a total repayment of 840,000 yuan. The principal and interest due for the Yu Ping Railway Public Bond winning tickets will be paid starting from November 30, 28th year of the Republic by the Central, China, and Communications Banks in various places. The principal and interest due for the Unified Public Bond, Series D, winning tickets will be paid starting from January 31, 29th year of the Republic, in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Finance, by the Central Bank in various places and the China and Communications Banks and the Central Trust Bureau entrusted by it. Now, please ask the supervisors to check the drawing tickets and the ledgers in order to execute the drawing.

Winning Numbers

After the supervisors checked the drawing tickets and the ledgers and found no errors, the representatives of the Central, China, and Communications Banks executed the drawing. The winning numbers are recorded as follows: (1) Eight branches of the Unified Public Bond, Series D: No. 004, No. 148, No. 278, No. 355, No. 533, No. 692, No. 763, No. 000. (2) Seven branches of the Yu Ping Railway Public Bond: No. 08, No. 22, No. 38, No. 62, No. 78, No. 89, No. 94. The Second Batch of Fractional Currency Notes Have Been Printed: Scheduled for Issuance Next Week; All Industries Feel the Need and It Is Difficult to Distribute; It Is Proposed That Each Firm Exchange 20 Yuan 75

After the Central Bank issued one-cent and five-cent fractional currency notes, the first batch has been completely issued. The second batch of 500,000 yuan (including 200,000 yuan in one-cent notes and 300,000 yuan in five-cent notes) was entrusted to the American company, Wing On Company, to print. It has completed the printing in batches and delivered it to the Central Bank in accordance with the contract. The bank has scheduled to continue issuing it starting next week. However, the issuance method is to entrust it to the trade associations of various industries for distribution. The general regulation is that each member firm of the association can exchange 20 yuan of fractional currency notes, with the aim of widespread circulation and preventing large amounts from flowing into the occupied areas. It is heard that the Shanghai trade associations have been registering the number of requests from members with the Shanghai branch of the Central Bank, amounting to no less than one hundred. The number applied for ranges from tens of thousands of yuan for the largest to thousands of yuan for the smallest. After receiving the letters, the Central Bank, because the 500,000 yuan of the second printing is really insufficient to meet the demand, yesterday specially replied to the trade associations, reducing the number of fractional currency notes registered for collection. The original letter said: "Respectfully, we have received your letter and learned that fractional currency notes are used for making change, and all industries feel the need. If all are exchanged in large quantities, our office will find it difficult to distribute. Regarding the request of your association's members to exchange fractional notes, we will consider allocating them at the appropriate time." After receiving the replies, the trade associations have also sent letters to their respective members, stating that they should not go to the trade association to apply before the Central Bank officially announces the date for collecting fractional currency notes, to avoid repeated trips.

Joint Order by Post Office and Customs: Regulations for Sending Small Parcels 78

The Shanghai Postal Administration and the Jianghai Customs have jointly established the following regulations for sending small parcel postal items: (1) Obtain a customs declaration form from the information desk, fill it out according to the format, and submit the customs declaration form to the information desk for stamping. (2) Inquire about the postage for the parcel at the registered or express window. (3) Submit the parcel to the customs inspection office for customs officers to inspect. (4) Go to the large parcel office upstairs to pay the applicable customs duties and purchase the required postage stamps. However, the parcel cannot be taken outside. For individual senders, it can be temporarily stored in the customs inspection office. (5) If it is a taxable small parcel, it is necessary to obtain a tax payment receipt from the tax payment office. (6) After affixing sufficient postage stamps to the small parcel, submit it to the customs inspection office for stamping. (7) Submit the small parcel to the registered or express window for posting and obtain a receipt for future reference. (8) If there are any unclear matters, inquiries can be made to the post office or customs.

Their intention in choosing this restaurant was to take advantage of the auspicious "Wanli" (ten thousand profits) name. A total of five tables were set up that day, with more than 40 guests attending. At 7:20 PM, just as the banquet was underway and everyone was enjoying themselves, three uninvited guests suddenly rushed in. Upon reaching the table, they each took out their handguns,

including Mauser pistols

And other weapons and fired more than ten shots continuously at the hosts, Yang Jinhai and Luo Zhibin. Yang was hit by a total of ten bullets, all in vital areas, and immediately fell to the ground dead. Luo was initially hit in the forehead by one bullet and fell. The assassins then added another shot to his back, causing him to die immediately as well. Although the assassins were in a hasty and panicked state, their bullets all concentrated on Yang and Luo, and none of the other people at the table were injured.

After the Incident

The Lao Zha (old gate) Police Station immediately received a report and detectives Zhang Keqin, Li Pengfei, and Huang Cifu rushed to the scene to make arrests. However, the assassins had already calmly fled, and most of the guests at the table with the two dead men scattered amidst the chaos. Those who remained were Pan Yasheng (an employee of the Japanese military police department) from Shanghai, Zhou Xilian, Yang Jinxi and Yang Shanfu from Zhenjiang, Yang Ganquan from Jiangbei, Zhang Jibin from Shanghai, Gui Qing, Wang Mingtang, Ji Dequan, He Yutang, Mi Henglong, and Wang Guanhua from Yangzhou, Zhu Daozhang and Zhang Chengzhi from Anhui, and Su Chengzhi, Li Zhuqing, and Zhou Gongzhao, totaling seventeen people. The detectives

Recovered Shell Casings

Twelve shell casings and five bullets from the scene. In addition to transporting the bodies of the two deceased to the coroner's office for examination, the seventeen remaining guests were considered suspects and subject to investigation. They were all taken to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Criminal Court of the Special No. 1 District Court. The police lawyer, Ru Bao, briefly explained the circumstances, stating that the seventeen suspects obtained were all related to this incident and required further investigation. If it was determined that they were not involved, the court was requested to release them. Currently, a petition was being made to

Approve Detention

For one week. According to rumors, this tragic event occurred entirely due to internal strife among Yang Jinhai and his associates. was forced to land by Japanese military aircraft while passing Zhou Island. Last night, the spokesperson of the Japanese Navy in Shanghai stated at a press briefing that the aircraft

Was forced to land because it flew into a prohibited area. At 9:30 AM that day, a Japanese military aircraft spotted the "Datanus" flying at an altitude of 670 feet, 5 miles away from Zhou Island. Most nations that treat our people with equality automatically abolish consular jurisdiction, demonstrating respect for our country's judiciary. Our country's government and people respect the rights and interests of foreigners even more. Even for stateless White Russian and Jewish refugees, our country has never harmed their legal rights and interests. Unexpectedly, Jewish refugees have recently followed in the footsteps of the great powers, undermining our country's legal authority by setting up a court in eastern Shanghai without authorization. The original text of lawyer Cai's letter to the Lawyers Association is recorded below: "Dear Sirs, I have learned that Jewish refugees, who were expelled from Germany and came to Shanghai, have recently organized a conciliation court without authorization at No. 66 Aierkaoke Road in eastern Shanghai. They have already begun handling cases and have established 15 articles of court regulations (full text attached). The main points are translated as follows: (1) Jewish people are prohibited from filing lawsuits in Chinese courts; otherwise, they will be punished. (2) Conciliation fees will be charged. (3) Lawyers registered with the court are allowed to appear in court. (4) Judgments do not apply Chinese law. (5) Judges and staff are formally appointed and receive salaries. This organization not only despises our country's courts but also undermines law and order. I specifically suggest that a thorough investigation and prevention should be conducted immediately. Sincerely, Member Cai Xiaobai," It is also known that the false court is currently scheduled to hear cases every Monday and Friday from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM. If the amount involved in a financial dispute is more than 500 yuan, a lawyer registered with the false court must be hired to appear in court.

Finance 95

Decline in Foreign Exchange Buying, US-British Exchange Rates Drop for Six Consecutive Days, Local Exchange Market Diverges

Yesterday's foreign exchange market saw no change in HSBC's listed rates. The informal market for US-British exchange was quiet due to the impending holiday. Trading was mediocre and the trend was slightly loose, as the various bullish sentiments that had permeated the market yesterday and the day before had gradually dissipated. Moreover, the widespread rumors of Germany's impending invasion of the Netherlands and Hitler's war rhetoric continued to shatter any illusions of peace in Europe. Consequently, overseas US-British exchange rates contracted further, falling by more than six points (after falling for six consecutive days, a total of 1.125 points). This caused the market to open with a familiar pattern of even British and tight US dollars. Soon after, Hong Kong banks and Chinese banks began selling. Although arbitrageurs initially seized the opportunity to buy on behalf of certain parties, the rate had already loosened to 5.21875 and 8.375. Subsequently, Chinese merchants and Sassoon also joined in the buying, pushing the rate back to 5.09375 and 8.1875. However, after that, Citibank, a foreign bank, offered to sell, and arbitrageurs also considered taking profits, causing the rate to harden again to 5.21875 and 8.28125. In the afternoon, the power company came to the market to settle accounts, momentarily tightening the rate to 5.09375 and 8.125. But after lingering for a long time, foreign banks suddenly began to sell. The closing price was still stable, with British gold at 5.1875 and the US exchange rate at 8.1875 (equivalent to a US-British exchange rate of only 3.788). Compared to the previous day, British exchange was looser by 0.125, while the US dollar was tighter by 0.03125. The futures market mirrored the spot market, with active trading throughout the day.

Hong Kong Banks Lead the Selling

At the beginning of the morning, London's forward and spot rates were even, the price of silver in New York remained flat, and the price of raw gold in London was unchanged. The exchange rate for British pounds against US dollars, Shanghai dollars, and French francs was flat. The US dollar continued to fall sharply against the British pound by six points, against the Shanghai dollar by 0.48 points, and against the French franc by a slight 0.031875 points. The Central Bank's listed rates remained unchanged. At the opening of the bank's spot selling prices, British gold was 5.0625, and the British exchange rate was 8.125. Compared to the previous close, British was even and the US dollar tightened by 0.09375, due to the sharp decline in the exchange rate. After the opening, Hong Kong Electric led the selling, and Chinese banks also came to sell. Although arbitrageurs seized the opportunity to buy on behalf of certain parties, the position was still quite ample, so the market ended up tightening. It is estimated that Hong Kong Electric sold spot British gold to arbitrageurs, HSBC, and other foreign banks at 5.125 and 5.1875, and spot US dollars from 8.25 to 8.3125. HSBC's listed rates were announced unchanged, and the Silver Equalization Tax was also announced unchanged. Thereafter, it was shouted up to 5.2875 and 8.375. Then Sassoon suddenly bought in, and at the same time, Chinese merchants also made purchases, so the trend suddenly turned tight. It is estimated that foreign banks, Citibank, and certain banks bought in spot British gold at 5.15625 and 5.125, and spot US dollars at 8.3125 and 8.25. Later, it was called down to 5.09375 and 8.1875. Near noon, the buying wind gradually subsided, and Citibank's selling intentions suddenly intensified, and British banks and arbitrageurs also resumed selling slightly, so the situation trended towards firmness again. It is estimated that they sold spot British gold to Chinese merchants and counterparts at 5.1875 and 5.21875, and spot US dollars at 8.25 and 8.28125. Extended to the noon close, the bank's spot selling price was British gold at 5.1875, and the US dollar at 8.25. Compared to the morning opening, the British exchange was looser by 0.125, and the US dollar rebounded by 0.125.

Power Company Settles Accounts

In the afternoon market, the market appearance once showed a tightening trend because the power company came to settle accounts, with British gold at 5.09375 and the US dollar reaching 8.125. After entering the market, the situation turned quiet, and the situation slightly rebounded. It was heard that Citibank sold spot US dollars to counterparts at 8.1875. Extended to the late close, the bank's spot selling price was British gold at 5.1875, and the US dollar at 8.1875. British gold for this month was 5.171875, and the US dollar was 8.15625. As a result, compared to the previous day, both spot and futures British were looser by 0.0125, while the US dollar was tighter by 0.03125.

Free Talk

Essays 111

— Pei Chu

The most prominent aspect of the modern spirit is probably "action." By "action," I mean being able to say it, being able to do it, not fearing any obstacles, and definitely achieving success. Our modern civilization is the result of the achievements of our predecessors' actions.

The day before yesterday, I also went to visit a Chinese language exhibition and felt another meaning of "action," which is about culture. In this exhibition, I spent the longest time looking at the Bible exhibited by the Bible Society. It not only exhibited Bibles in various languages from all over the world for us to see, but also exhibited Bibles in various dialects of China. Among them, in addition to the Ningbo, Xiamen, or other city dialects that we easily see, there are also Bibles in special dialects from the southwest, northwest, and northeast regions of China. We have almost never heard of these dialects. I really cannot but admire the spirit of action of the Western missionaries!

For us, Western missionaries are just like our monks and Taoists, whose profession is to preach and who do not engage in secular affairs. Since they are otherworldly people, in our opinion, they are just like our monks and Taoists, who can just practice tranquility and enjoy blessings without having to plan too much and ask for trouble. However, they are not like that. They want to act. They can not only go deep into barren and dangerous places to preach their doctrines, but also promote culture in these places at the same time. They published these Bibles in special dialects! They, as missionaries, are already doing so much. Needless to say, those non-missionaries who specialize in secular affairs work even harder. No wonder they surpass us in both spirit and material things.

Therefore, I turned around and thought about ourselves. There are many things that we should do, but aren't we hindering them, making people afraid to act, or being constrained and giving up on them? Let's not talk about other things, but take the new writing system as an example. It is almost the same thing as the Bible in special dialects. What achievements have we made? Why are we so far behind them? And this work of special dialects is precisely what we should be responsible for.

However, I am not trying to make pessimistic or disappointing remarks after all. We all know how to act now, and many things are being done, or are being done. Language exhibition can be said to be a kind of action!

Mother 112

— Xiao Ping

The noisy sounds of the street gradually sank into the night.

Rain—endlessly falling on the silent streets.

From the dimly lit and weary street lamps, I vaguely saw slender strands of rain. October 29th was quietly dragged away by the god of night, and the 30th struggled to come in the darkness.

It was such a quiet autumn rainy night that I hurriedly stepped on messy steps, stepping over the road that had been wetted by hundreds, thousands, and millions of tiny raindrops, and hurried home.

The shops with iron doors tightly closed slowly receded around me, and soon I was approaching my home.

Two dark circles, a stern mother's face, appeared before my eyes. She was depressed because of her daughter's late return; at this time, listening to the frequent sad sound of the rain, she anxiously and resentfully missed her daughter who had not yet returned home.

I clearly realized that she was suffering from her daughter's "change," and sometimes she couldn't bear it and would angrily lash out at her beloved daughter unintentionally. But I love her, without any hatred for her. Mother is the mother I will always love. Mother said that I am a girl, so how can I go far away? But girls should also have a bright future in this era. It will never be like my mother's era...

But I don't intend to leave her either.

Because of my father's early death, she struggled to raise her daughter—me—in a difficult and weak life. She often shed tears for her unhealthy and sickly daughter. For more than ten years, the feudal family only gave her coldness, disdain, and coercion; she had tasted the pain of the world. Her only daughter can comfort her, and her hope is also closely tied to her daughter, hoping to live a happy life in the future.

Now——

She is disappointed. Her daughter is gradually deviating from her hopes, shattering her many years of expectations for her daughter.

Mother's bitter face brought me depression. I was always thinking about how I could comfort my most beloved mother in the world? I can't make her wounded heart suffer again. Once, and once again, and again, I failed.

Pain pierced my heart, and my mind was full of doubts. How can I persuade my mother, and that day when my mother can understand her daughter and become Gorky's "Mother"?

I wandered on the street like this. The rain was still so drizzly.

Autumn and the Cold River 113

— Ding Ti

As long as I close my eyes, I cannot forget. A piece of virtual white floats on my eyes, the light is not dazzling, but it is so elegant, quiet, and gentle. It is as if I can imagine a vast and boundless river, where the sky and water meet, and the clear light is rendered on the painting, a piece of azure blue and a strip of green. The god crows and village drums have not been seen for many years, and spiders secretly fill the house with their formations. Under the thick dust, the vermilion paint of the pillars is buried. You can smell the bird droppings all over the ground. Occasionally, a few tiles fall beside the Buddhist shrine, covered with dust. A silent bell is sent from afar, and then you lean your body and listen to the sparrows chirping on the beams. It seems that autumn comes from the north of the river, or from the cold river. People living in the river city feel autumn earlier, and a dilapidated mountain is most suitable for autumn. When the reeds are blown by the wind and rise and fall with a rustling sound, when the boundless leaves of the villages are dyed yellow, you see everyone on the streets of the river city wearing thick padded jackets. There are few tourists in the temples in the dilapidated mountains all day long, and the stone benches and tables in the pavilions are even colder than ice. If you are clever, don't sit down. The new weather is clear and bright, the clear river is like a practice, and the desolation of the cold river brings a city of autumn, ...

Suddenly the calm waves trembled. There was such a day, when the night was dark and the wind was high, we heard the cries of many innocent people. In October, on a sailboat, on the north and south banks of the river, I spent more than ten days on the river. In the night sky dotted with starlight, the huge figure of the pagoda cast a shadow on the gray river. At night, we could hear the roaring waves hitting the boat, one wave after another. In the bleak morning when the mountain mist first opened, the mountains were green, the wind was high, and the sky was urgent. I couldn't say I loved the cold river anymore, and my heart was shrinking and I couldn't feel a trace of warmth. In the pale dawn of the reeds, thin branches swayed in the gray sky, and a dog barked in the cold. The deck was slippery, as if covered with a thin layer of ice. The dark shadows of the jungle surrounded a small village; there were sparse lights in the board door, and one or two "kerosene lamps" were also lit at the cable boat under the bridge, flickering in the square doorway. The sharp night wind, like scissors, passed through the cracks in the ship's planks and stung the face. Occasionally, looking out the window, it was a piece of silent darkness. Does the water of my hometown not flow here? Everyone wanted to explore all the unknown mysteries from the dark shadows, but they were all disappointed. The harbor of the river is winding, and the twists and turns are a bit strange. In front, behind, left, and right of the village, there is a vast expanse of water. Pointing the pole, the boat swung over, and the old man in the east helped the child on the west bank into the house. Day by day, the leaves on the shore were yellower than before, and people wearing cotton robes still had to bask in the sun. The river wind was biting, and the river water was even colder. Ten days of life on the boat consumed the remaining autumn without a trace. You say that is also a peaceful autumn, a cold river with a fluke of autumn? Ah, no, no. In a moment of drifting on the cold river, in the bleak October, I wrote the words "homesickness" on the river, on the yellow leaves of autumn. I miss Jiangcheng. I cannot forget a state of mind of autumn, the autumn river, the melancholy on the river.

I have spent two autumns, in this big city. When the spire of the church seems more gloomy in the evening wind, the autumn on the river is also deep. Flowing in the streets of towering buildings, the wind roars, rolling into a vortex like a swift current. On the streets near the Bund, the sunlight is as thin as winter. The wind on the river brings distant dreams, and a layer of virtual white floats on my eyes, and then a pile of melancholy, like dark clouds. On the shore where battleships and giant ships are crowded, I can see that piece of river, the autumn on the cold river.

Piled up in the thick dust, for many years the peaceful river, autumn, Jiangcheng, the god crows and village drums, under the shrine of Fo Li, ... I cannot say I love the cold river anymore. In the bleak October weather, on the vast river, the night of the waves, the morning of the frost, life is like an ant running around on a hot pot, that drifting bitterness! From the small city with dim lights on the water to a big city by the sea, I searched everywhere for the lost autumn. Autumn comes from the cold river, it is deep and then remains, one year, two years, three years. Maybe you can imagine a bit of the scenery of your hometown Jiangcheng from the Bund, but what about the lost autumn—from the disturbance, where should you take back a share of peace?

Introduction to "A Brief History of Late Qing Small Newspapers" 114

— Ru Hui

There has never been a precise statistic on how many kinds of small newspapers there were in the late Qing Dynasty. According to the existing documents, Li Chuang Woluo Sheng's "Illustrated Anecdotes of Shanghai for Leisurely Reading" (1905) said that there were ten kinds of newspapers "using playful writing to provide people with leisure." The list is as follows:

Prosperity Daily, Laughing Forest Daily, Game Daily, Leisure Daily, Fable Daily, Collection Daily

New Shanghai Daily, Flower World, Flowery Days Daily, Spring River Flower Moon Daily

Nan Ting Ting Zhang's "List of Lost Newspapers in Shanghai" (1906) listed more, a total of sixty-six kinds. However, most of them are still newspapers that report current events. Only the following twelve kinds can be determined as small newspapers:

Art Forest Daily, Strange News Daily, Strange New Daily, Laughing Daily, Handbook Daily, Flying Daily

Spring River Flower Moon Daily, Laughing Daily, Interesting Daily, China Small Daily, Leisure Daily, Literature Club

Daily

Combined with the "Miscellaneous Records of Leisurely Reading," there are a total of twenty kinds. Later works on the history of newspapers also occasionally touched on this, but they only briefly mentioned the numbers of "Prosperity," "Games," "Fables," and "Collection." Unexpectedly, I accidentally obtained seven kinds that were not found in the lists of Woluo Sheng and Nan Ting Ting Zhang:

Entertainment Leisure Daily, Romance Vernacular Daily, Dialect Daily, Suzhou Vernacular Daily, Popular

News, Auspicious Shadows Daily, and Live in the Moment Daily

A total of twenty-seven kinds. This is the largest known number of small newspapers at that time. Among the twenty-seven kinds, the following seven have not been found: "New Shanghai," "Flower World," "Art Forest," "Strange News," "Strange New," "Laughing," and "Handbook." I am afraid that even the already found parts will eventually be lost, so I will describe the outlines of the twenty kinds that have been obtained to preserve them.

The Shaky God of Peace 115

Entertainment Circle

Derogatory Films will Disappear, Hollywood Understands China, Changing Styles is the Gift of the War of Resistance 116

— Xin Ying

In the past, we knew that Hollywood film companies often had many misunderstandings about China, and derogatory films could often be found. Even in films with derogatory content, they would find Chinese actors to play humiliating roles. Didn't Anna May Wong play many such roles in the past?

But now, Hollywood film companies have realized the non-counting nature of this policy, because Hollywood films have a large market in China. If you transport this kind of film to China for screening, it will cause Chinese people's aversion. The things China has performed in the film are inconsistent with the facts. China is an ancient country that was civilized earliest, and she has an indelible splendid culture.

On the other hand, Chinese actors have also thoroughly realized in recent years that they only knew how to earn wages in the past, and everything was arranged by the producers or directors. They were asked to play what kind of role, and they played what kind of role. They didn't know anything about insulting China. Now, they know that playing this kind of role is insulting to their motherland, which will not only make their compatriots dissatisfied, but also affect their own future. Therefore, they have paid attention to this issue. In the future, when they encounter companies asking them to play derogatory roles, they will politely refuse.

Under this situation, Hollywood film companies will not only avoid making films with derogatory content in the future, but also decide not to have Chinese actors play roles such as child slaves and servants. This will eliminate disputes or misunderstandings caused by the public screening of films in China. And we believe that this war of resistance in China has changed the entire world, seeing that China is the largest country in the Far East with unlimited prospects. This is indeed a major reason for accelerating Hollywood's change of this policy!

Chaplin Participates in the War of Resistance 117

— Hua Zhi

"The Dictator," starring the screen comedian Chaplin, has been rumored for more than a year. The central consciousness of the film portrays a certain dictator in Europe as a poor little soldier, which inevitably causes international trouble. The film production has been suspended several times. Whenever Chaplin wants to continue filming, a secret group will warn him with threats to take his life. Chaplin has to add and delete content and rename it "The Great Dictator," but he still has no intention of completing it. After the start of the European War, the situation is of course different. Chaplin also became motivated and prepared to join the democratic front to fight for the Jews. In view of the fact that British and French film actors have returned to their countries to join the army, he recently closed himself in the Kemala room, buried himself in filming, working ten hours day and night, preparing to finish it quickly and increase the power of publicity. When Chaplin is filming, the guards outside the door are heavily guarded, with ten armed guards to prevent people from breaking in and disrupting. It is said that this film will instill political consciousness, not just satire. Chaplin also told a friend: "In short, Hitler is no laughing matter." Some news reporters believe that Chaplin has made a great determination to resist the war, and "The Dictator" will be his last work. After that, he will imitate the famous Shakespearean actor Sir Gielgud in Britain and join the British infantry and set off for the front line. If this is true, then Charlie Chaplin, the comedian of thirty years, has completely changed his style.

Recent News from Storytelling Theaters 118

— Di Sheng

Xu Yunzhi recently started singing the new book "Hetongji" at Yalu Teahouse "Rimen." This book is taken from the Yue opera story of the true and false Wang Qingming. The Tan Huang theaters often perform it, which can attract audiences; and Xu is the pioneer in adapting it to string and wind instruments. It is said that the "script" is written by a certain chapter novel writer. Although the structure of the plot is generally not bad, the "chapter" is still not stable and is inevitably mediocre. It should be regarded as the same level as Zhu Zhao's "Crying and Laughing Marriage," so the old listeners have mixed praise and criticism for it.

Pin Fang recruited Kang Youhua, a famous artist from Kuanyi Society, to tell the Yangzhou book "Romance of the Three Kingdoms," which reduced a good base for female storytellers in Puyu Society.

The Fuchun Night Teahouse is still closed. Recently, "Miao Wang" Xia Hesheng volunteered to recruit famous artists, and there is news that the night teahouse will reopen soon. Xia has done "New Year's file" in Fuchun this spring, and his reputation is not bad, which has achieved good results. This time, he has considerable confidence in the box office for "reopening the file."

Employees of Guangyu and Runyu Societies have always been very enthusiastic about public welfare undertakings. Now that all walks of life in Shanghai are enthusiastically raising donations for winter clothes, the colleagues of the two societies have also initiated a large-scale singing association, storytelling association, and series opera activities to respond and raise donations on a large scale.

Dance troupe writing shadows

— Xiao Tian

Life 119

I remember one day when I watched a drama at the Xuan Palace. When the curtain opened, there was a dancer living in the front room, with many modern furniture arranged. The dancer sat on a soft sofa, listening to the radio, talking to guests on the phone, and enjoying material civilization as much as possible. A country girl lived in the back pavilion, and a dying old woman was lying on a broken bed. The second landlord was chasing her like his life to ask her to pay the rent she owed. The country girl didn't know what to do, so she suddenly ran to the front room to ask the dancer for some help, to think of a way out for her to maintain her life. But the dancer loudly asked, do you want to live or live? If you want to live, you should persevere in maintaining the ambition you have set, and what does it matter if you are a little embarrassed or hungry. If you want to live, what you can sell now is your flesh. (The general idea is like this.) At that time, there were several dancers in the audience who frequently wiped their eyes with handkerchiefs, probably shedding tears of sympathy.

"I did evil in my previous life, and I am a dancer in this life." Even the red star with a monthly income of more than a thousand yuan also said so. However, in the eyes of a group of poor women, dancers eat delicacies, wear woolen silk, and there are many gentlemen and young masters who pursue and flatter them. What's so bad about that? Alas, swallow the broken teeth into your stomach, and you know the suffering yourself. Currently, at the Paramount, there are two red stars who told me that I really believe and sympathize with their plight. A friend objected, "You are not a dancer, how do you know the suffering of dancers?" I said, "You are not me, how do you know I don't know the suffering of dancers?" This is just copying the old article of Mr. Zhuang, but unfortunately that friend doesn't understand, and he still wants to ask the two red stars to testify.

According to this, is it possible for dancers to only seek to live and not to live? No, no, there are many prominent people who drive in high carriages and驷, but they are not living, they are just living luxuriously. The Western philosopher said, "People eat to live, not live to eat." Therefore, the two words "life" must be put together to have meaning, otherwise it will become a walking dead. But this is a question of knowledge, not a question of occupation. In any industry, there are virtuous people and there are scoundrels. Confucius said, "At fifteen, I set my heart on learning, and at thirty I stood firm..." Dancers, do you want to live? You should first humbly study, learn some knowledge, learn the principles of being a human being. When you discover the bright road of life, you will definitely have the joy and ambition to move forward, and you will no longer feel world-weariness and distress.

Unofficial History of the Pear Garden 120

— Xu Muyun

A Drama that Praises National Heroes

Chinese dramas are mostly entertaining in nature. There are also many who advocate old virtues such as loyalty, filial piety, and righteousness, but there are very few who praise national heroes and can be called national defense dramas. There is a Kunqu opera called "Ningwu Pass," also known as "A Family of Martyrs," which does meet the above two conditions. However, the lyrics are profound and the music is high and few can sing it. Kunqu opera is gradually declining and on the verge of extinction. On the contrary, Pihuang, which has a shorter history, can be popularized throughout the country and is warmly welcomed by people of all levels. Therefore, it is a pity that there is such a good drama, which can also be adapted to the ideological trend of modern times, but it is buried and gradually forgotten by the world. If drama lovers do not actively promote it, I am afraid that within a few years, there will be a lament for the loss of good works and the dispersal of songs in Guangling. Therefore, I am now specially narrating the plot of the drama to arouse the attention of the Chinese people. If playwrights can adapt it into Pihuang and have a capable bearded male lead actor who is proficient in both martial arts and literature perform it, it is expected that it will inspire people's hearts today and gain the warm approval of the audience.

In the late Ming Dynasty, eunuchs monopolized power and politics were corrupt. Although Emperor Chongzhen was not a monarch who brought about the downfall of the country, the imperial government had deteriorated to the point where it could not be remedied. Traitors deceived the emperor, and heavy taxes were levied. The roving bandits rose up everywhere, and the Qing soldiers took advantage of the opportunity to invade from outside. The rebellious thieves disturbed from within. Even with the wisdom of Emperor Sizong, the general trend was gone and could not be reversed. Among the officials, only the eunuch Wang Chengen and the general Li Guozhen were wholeheartedly devoted to the country and sacrificed themselves for the country after Yuan Chonghuan. (138)

Amateur Music Concert 121

— Ru Yun

At 8 pm on the 19th of this month, there will be a grand music concert at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA. The participants in this music concert include the best amateur musicians in Shanghai, the Conservatory of Music, and the singing classes of various amateur groups, all with their best personnel participating. It can also be said that this "Shanghai Amateur Music Circle Concert" is a total mobilization of amateur music talents in Shanghai.

In terms of programs, there are solo piano, violin, guitar, etc., ensemble and solo singing, etc. The most eye-catching is the large chorus of more than one hundred people, which gathers the essence of each group. The program to be sung has been decided to be Huang Zi's posthumous work, but which song has not yet been decided. It is probably nothing more than "The Flag is Flying" and "The Hunt."

In terms of ticket prices, there are two types: one yuan and two yuan. This is because the YMCA does not have many seats originally, and some of them have to be reserved for the performers themselves, so it has to be like this. In addition to being sold at the venue on the day of the event, tickets were also sold in advance to all walks of life, so it is probably no problem to be full.

Since Shanghai became an "isolated island," small-scale concerts of a recreational nature have been held from time to time, but this is the first time that the elites of the entire music world have gathered together. It symbolizes the unity of the amateur music world on the "isolated island," and it is the starting point for establishing the expansion from quantity to quality.
